Special Solicitation

Rationalization of Commissions 246

Now, a certain large local newspaper intends to add a few colleagues to its advertising department. Academic degrees are not important, but at least a high school diploma is required, so that they will not feel difficult when handling affairs. Naturally, it would be best if they had experience in soliciting advertisements in the past, otherwise, as long as they are willing to work diligently under the guidance of others, they will be able to fulfill their duties happily. Room and board can be provided by the newspaper, but there is no monthly salary, it is entirely based on commissions. However, the rules for these commissions are very rational. The more you work hard, the higher the commission. The scale of this newspaper is naturally not as large as the Shen and Xin newspapers, but it is already on a considerable foundation, and the future is very promising. However, soliciting advertisements is not a very refined matter, you must have patience, be able to endure hardship, and not be afraid of being "rejected! rejected!" by the heads of trading firms, in order to find happiness from struggle. Friends who are interested in entering the newspaper industry, please write to discuss it. Please be sure to attach a resume in the letter so that we can discuss it with the manager in advance, and there will always be a reply whether it is successful or not. Please send your letters to Mr. Di, No. 367, Taipingfang, Sanmalu (Third Avenue) for forwarding.

Quick Guide to Life Republished 247

Since the first edition of Quick Guide to Life sold out five days ago, there has been an overwhelming number of mail orders. The 10,000-copy reprint has now been published. The content is rich, combining the essence of calendars, whole books, yearbooks, guides, and other books, so it meets the needs of home and travel. Each copy is only sold for 20 cents of silver. Biographies

Hoover's Childhood (Middle) 248

— Wu Huifen

Three years passed quickly, and Hoover was seventeen years old. At that time, Senator Stanford of the United States established Stanford University in California, and he went to register for the entrance examination. Unfortunately, because he had studied mathematics and science on his own, his level was lacking, and he did not pass the exam. Just as he was feeling unhappy, he met a professor who took pity on his situation, hired him as an assistant, and told him to specialize in geology at Stanford University.

Because his circumstances were poor, Hoover had to work to support himself. Therefore, he worked on farms early in the morning, or worked as a newspaper vendor, went to the university to listen to lectures during the day, and worked hard for others at night. He did this every day, without interruption. Until he graduated from the Mining and Metallurgy Department of Stanford University at the age of twenty-one. Although he did not have very good grades, he was still a Bachelor of Engineering.

At that time, he should have had a job, but because people from the University of California and Stanford University competed for positions, the mines in the California area were all occupied by graduates from the University of California, and graduates from Stanford University could not find a suitable opportunity. Hoover's fate was certainly no different, but he didn't think it was strange. He thought, "If I can't be a technician, I can always be a miner." So he entered the Nevada Mine as a miner.

His job was to transport ore, moving it from inside the pit to outside the pit. If he did not do it well or too slowly, he would be scolded by the workers in the pit.

Fortunately, a talented person will not be buried for life. In less than a year, his knowledge was appreciated by a famous mining technician named Hoffman, who introduced him to a famous industrialist, Lord Henning. Henning also recognized Hoover's abilities and introduced him to a wealthy Englishman who was running a mine in Western Australia and needed a technician to study the geology of the Australian mine. At that time, Hoover was twenty-three years old.

From then on, Hoover's fate gradually unfolded step by step. Two years later, he returned from Western Australia and married Henry, a female classmate from Stanford University. At that time, because of his outstanding achievements in geological surveys over the years, his reputation also grew, and soon he was hired by our country to be the chief mining technician of our country. In 1901, when he was twenty-seven years old, he came to China for the second time, planning the transformation of foreign-invested enterprises and engaging in the construction of railways and harbors. After that, he was entrusted by mine groups operated by large European and American capitalists to investigate the ore veins around the world. At that time, Hoover was not only an American mining technician, but had also become the world-famous only mining technician.

From Hoover's hard study and hard work to becoming a mining technician, all of this happened before the World War. As for the path he took from the industrial world to the political world, it began when the Great War broke out.

In 1915, to commemorate the opening of the Panama Canal, the World Expo was held in San Francisco, USA. Hoover was sent to Europe to persuade the United Kingdom, France, Germany, and other countries to participate together. Soon, the European War broke out. At that time, it was the hot summer, and there were as many as 160,000 Americans traveling and sightseeing in Europe. When the European War began, they all felt considerable danger and did not know how to return to the United States, which became a big problem. At that time, Hoover accepted the commission of the American ambassador to the United Kingdom and was appointed as the chairman of the American People's Relief Committee, responsible for handling this matter. Hoover used his quick and skillful methods to send this large group of Americans back to their country very easily. As a result, Hoover was highly respected by the American people! Not only that, but Hoover also went on to rescue Belgian refugees who had been ravaged by the German army and left homeless, saving ten million people from starvation. This kind of thing made the Europeans feel a special kind of gratitude to the United States, and Hoover's methods were also recognized by the world.
